     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_placement">Battery placement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Battery placement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In contrast to most other <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicles</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Roadster" title="Tesla Roadster">Roadster</a>, the battery pack of the Model S forms the floor of the vehicle between the axles, providing the vehicle with several advantages. Most notably, since the battery pack is the single heaviest component of the vehicle, the Model S has a <a href="/wiki/Center_of_gravity" title="Center of gravity">center of gravity</a> height of only 18 inches (46&nbsp;cm),<sup id="cite_ref-rope_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rope-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sciAbuild_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciAbuild-111">[105]</a></sup> helping it to achieve a <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_car#Lateral_acceleration" title="Formula One car">lateral acceleration</a> of 0.9g<sup id="cite_ref-youtube_RWQ_dnpplaA_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube_RWQ_dnpplaA-112">[106]</a></sup> and good protection against <a href="/wiki/Rollover" title="Rollover">rollover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gcsafe_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcsafe-114">[108]</a></sup> Secondly, the absence of a heavy engine between the front or rear axle allows the bulk of the <a href="/wiki/Mass_distribution" title="Mass distribution">mass to be centralized</a> between the axles, lowering <a href="/wiki/Rotational_inertia" title="Rotational inertia" class="mw-redirect">rotational inertia</a> allowing it to turn more quickly. Thirdly, the placement of the battery pack increases the rigidity of the passenger compartment, improving the passive safety of the vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[109]</a></sup> Fourth, placing the battery pack under the vehicle makes it possible to remove or replace the entire unit in 90 seconds,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[110]</a></sup> either for maintenance or for Tesla's Battery Swap service.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charger">Charger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Charger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Charing_port_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The Model S charge port is located in front of the left taillight.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_store,_Austin,_Texas_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg/220px-Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg/330px-Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg/440px-Tesla_store%2C_Austin%2C_Texas_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_store,_Austin,_Texas_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Model S charging connectors at the Tesla store in 
        <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Model S comes equipped with a different charger and connector in North American vs. European markets, reflecting differences in the local electric grid.</p> 
     <p>In all markets the charge port is located behind a door in the left taillight. During charging, the charge port pulses green. The frequency at which the charge port's light pulses slows down as the charge level approaches full. When charging is complete, the light stops pulsing and is solid green.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[111]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <p>The standard North American onboard charger accepts single phase 120 or 240-volt sources at a rate of up to <span class="nowrap">10 kW</span>. Included adapters allow the car to charge from a standard 120 volt outlet, a 240 volt NEMA 14-50 outlet, and <a href="/wiki/SAE_J1772" title="SAE J1772">SAE J1772</a> public chargers. An optional <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,000</span> upgrade for a second <span class="nowrap">10 kW</span> onboard charger supports a total of up to <span class="nowrap">20 kW</span> charging from an <span class="nowrap">80 amp</span> available <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$750</span> Tesla Wall Connector.<sup id="cite_ref-MT20120622_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MT20120622-4">[4]</a></sup> The North American connector uses a proprietary Tesla design.</p> 
     <p>Charging times vary depending on the battery pack's state-of-charge, its overall capacity, the available voltage, and the available <a href="/wiki/Circuit_breaker" title="Circuit breaker">circuit breaker</a> amperage. From a 120 volt/15 amp household outlet, the range increases by 3.75 miles (6&nbsp;km) for every hour of charging. From a <span class="nowrap">10 kW</span>, <a href="/wiki/AC_power_plugs_and_sockets#NEMA_14-50" title="AC power plugs and sockets">NEMA 14–50</a> 240 V/50 A outlet (like those used by <a href="/wiki/RVs" title="RVs" class="mw-redirect">RVs</a> or standard cooking ranges), the charge rate is 28.75 miles (46&nbsp;km) per hour. Using Tesla's <span class="nowrap">20 kW</span>, <span class="nowrap">240 V</span> High Power Wall Connector increases the rate to 57 miles (92&nbsp;km) per hour if the car is configured with twin chargers (<span class="nowrap">20 kW</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-TMCharging_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCharging-118">[112]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_.2F_Asia_Pacific">Europe / Asia Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Europe / Asia Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg/220px-Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg/330px-Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg/440px-Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla-type-2-model-s-charge-port-inlet-0996.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Type 2-compatible inlet on European Model S
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The standard European charger accepts three phase <span class="nowrap">230 V</span> or <span class="nowrap">400 V</span> at up to <span class="nowrap">11 kW</span>. The <a href="/wiki/Type_2_connector" title="Type 2 connector">Type 2 connector</a> on the car directly accepts "Mennekes" <a href="/wiki/IEC_62196" title="IEC 62196">IEC 62196</a> charging from public stations at up to 400 V, and included adapters allow the car to charge from standard continental European outlets and <a href="/wiki/IEC_60309" title="IEC 60309">IEC 60309</a> 230 volt (blue 3-pin) or 400 volt (red 5-pin) outlets, depending on region. The addition of a second charger supports charging at up to 22&nbsp;kW, and the Tesla Wall Connector was stated for be available from last-2015.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[113]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Superchargers">Superchargers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Superchargers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg/220px-Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg/330px-Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg/440px-Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla-type-2-supercharger-outlet-1004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Type 2-compatible outlet found on 
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_supercharger" title="Tesla supercharger" class="mw-redirect">Tesla superchargers</a> in Europe
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Tesla built 120&nbsp;kW<sup id="cite_ref-TMSuperchargerPower_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMSuperchargerPower-120">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tesla_supercharger" title="Tesla supercharger" class="mw-redirect">Tesla supercharger</a> stations to allow long distance travel in North America, Europe, Asia, and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-TMSuperCharger_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMSuperCharger-121">[115]</a></sup> A Supercharger can add up to 125 miles (201&nbsp;km) of range in 20 minutes and a full charge in approximately one hour assuming a nearly empty <span class="nowrap">85 kWh</span> battery.<sup id="cite_ref-MT20120622_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MT20120622-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMCharging_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCharging-118">[112]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Supercharging hardware is included in the 85&nbsp;kWh, 70&nbsp;kWh, and 60&nbsp;kWh battery packs; in both the 85&nbsp;kWh models and 70&nbsp;kWh models,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[116]</a></sup> the payment for the car includes supercharging by default, but in the 60&nbsp;kWh, supercharging was software-disabled and one must pay an extra fee to enable supercharging.<sup id="cite_ref-TMOptions_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMOptions-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMCharging_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMCharging-118">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TMGear_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMGear-123">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[118]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension">Suspension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Suspension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The Model S has <a href="/wiki/Independent_suspension" title="Independent suspension">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Coil_spring" title="Coil spring">coil spring</a> suspension on all four wheels – front <a href="/wiki/Double_wishbone_suspension" title="Double wishbone suspension">double wishbone</a>, virtual steer axis <a href="/wiki/Control_arm" title="Control arm">control arm</a> and rear independent <a href="/wiki/Multi-link_suspension" title="Multi-link suspension">multilink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-model_s_specs_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-model_s_specs-49">[49]</a></sup> As an extra-cost option, the car is available with <a href="/wiki/Self-leveling_suspension" title="Self-leveling suspension" class="mw-redirect">self-leveling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Height_adjustable_suspension" title="Height adjustable suspension">height-adjustable</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_suspension" title="Air suspension">air suspension</a>. This is accomplished via adjustable Bilstein shock absorbers controlled by the driver. The car is meant to lower itself at highway speed and raise itself to traverse steep driveways and rough terrain, despite the low 6-inch <a href="/wiki/Ground_clearance" title="Ground clearance" class="mw-redirect">ground clearance</a> and rather long 116-inch wheelbase.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[119]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Because, in the Tesla, electronic systems can be upgraded by "over-the-air" download, rather than recall, the suspension system has been changed retroactively on several occasions. During the 2013 'fire investigation', <a href="/wiki/NHTSA" title="NHTSA" class="mw-redirect">NHTSA</a> asked Tesla to disable the car's ability to lower itself at speed on the theory that a ground clearance below 6 inches might cause the batteries underneath the car to contact road debris.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[120]</a></sup> In September 2014, Tesla upgraded the <a href="/wiki/Height_adjustable_suspension" title="Height adjustable suspension">height adjustment feature</a> for Model S cars equipped with air suspension to remember locations that require higher clearance such as those with potholes and steep driveways, and automatically adjusts to avoid them.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[121]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autopilot">Autopilot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Autopilot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Beginning with vehicles manufactured in late September 2014, all new Model S vehicles come equipped with a camera mounted at the top of the windshield, forward looking radar in the lower grill, and ultrasonic <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_location" title="Acoustic location">acoustic location</a> sensors in the front and rear bumpers that provide a 360-degree buffer zone around the car. This equipment allows Model S to detect road signs, lane markings, obstacles, and other vehicles. In addition to <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_cruise_control" title="Adaptive cruise control" class="mw-redirect">adaptive cruise control</a> and lane departure warning, a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,500</span> "Tech Package" option will allow this system to enable semi-autonomous drive and parking capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[124]</a></sup> New models sold since October 9, 2014 have the option to have Autopilot, which allows <a href="/wiki/Hands-free_driving" title="Hands-free driving" class="mw-redirect">hands-free driving</a> in many situations. AutoPilot-enabled cars receive software updates for the AutoPilot software wirelessly, just as all other Model S cars receive general software updates wirelessly.</p> 
     <p>In mid October 2015 in the U.S. Tesla rolled out version 7 of their software that included autopilot capability.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[125]</a></sup> On January 9, 2016, Tesla rolled out version 7.1 as an <a href="/wiki/Over-the-air_programming" title="Over-the-air programming">over-the-air</a> update, adding a new "summon" feature that allows cars to self-park at parking locations without the driver in the car.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[126]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Some industry experts have raised questions about the legal status of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_driving" title="Autonomous driving" class="mw-redirect">autonomous driving</a> in the U.S. and whether Model S owner would violate current state regulations when using the autopilot function. The few states that have passed laws allowing autonomous cars on the road limit their use for testing purposes, not the use by the general public. Also, there are questions about the liability for autonomous cars in case there is a mistake.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTautopilot_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTautopilot-133">[127]</a></sup> A Tesla spokesman said there is "nothing in our autopilot system that is in conflict with current regulations." "We are not getting rid of the pilot. This is about releasing the driver from tedious tasks so they can focus and provide better input." <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s director of self-driving cars at the company said he does not think there is a regulatory block as far as the self-driving vehicle met crash-test and other safety standards. A spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) said that "any autonomous vehicle would need to meet applicable federal motor vehicle safety standards" and the NHTSA "will have the appropriate policies and regulations in place to ensure the safety of this type of vehicles."<sup id="cite_ref-NYTautopilot_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTautopilot-133">[127]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to Elon Musk, the Model S was designed to be a computer on wheels: ""We really designed the Model S to be a very sophisticated computer on wheels. Tesla is a software company as much as it is a hardware company. A huge part of what Tesla is, is a Silicon Valley software company. We view this the same as updating your phone or your laptop.""<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[128]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to Musk, "the car <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">will learn over time</a>", including from other cars.<sup id="cite_ref-learn_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-learn-135">[129]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instrument_panel">Instrument panel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Instrument panel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_digital_panels.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Production dashboard with main dashboard digital display (left) and central 17-inch (430&nbsp;mm) 
        <a href="/wiki/Touchscreen" title="Touchscreen">touchscreen</a> control panel (right)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The instrument panel is a 12.3-inch (31&nbsp;cm) <a href="/wiki/Liquid-crystal_display" title="Liquid-crystal display">liquid-crystal display</a> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_instrument_cluster" title="Electronic instrument cluster">electronic instrument cluster</a> that indicates speed, power usage, charge level, estimated range and active gear, as well as Nav directions (driven by <a href="/wiki/Garmin" title="Garmin">Garmin</a>). The gearbox can be set to Drive, Neutral, Reverse and Park. The <a href="/wiki/Infotainment" title="Infotainment">infotainment</a> control <a href="/wiki/Touchscreen" title="Touchscreen">touchscreen</a> is a 17-inch (43&nbsp;cm) <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a> panel divided into four areas. A top line displays status symbols and provides shortcuts to Charging, <a href="/wiki/HomeLink" title="HomeLink" class="mw-redirect">HomeLink</a>, Driver Profiles, vehicle information (software version and the <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_identification_number" title="Vehicle identification number">Vehicle identification number</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a>. The second line provides access to several apps including Media, Nav (driven by <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a>, and thus is separate from the Nav on instrument panel), Energy, Web, Camera and Phone. The central main viewing area displays the (two) active apps, subdivided into upper and lower areas. (Most apps can be expanded to take up the entire area). At the bottom is access to various controls and settings for the vehicle such as doors, locks and lights as well as temperature controls and a secondary volume control.</p> 
     <p>The instrument cluster and the infotainment panel are driven by separate <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> <a href="/wiki/Tegra_3" title="Tegra 3" class="mw-redirect">Tegra 3</a> <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D Visual Computing</a> Modules.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[131]</a></sup> Tesla was the first company to ship this technology. (<a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> later delivered this technology in its 2013 model year in Europe, and in North America in 2014.)<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[132]</a></sup> The Tegra <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">system on a chip</a> (SoC) integrates eight specialized processors, including a <a href="/wiki/Multi-core" title="Multi-core" class="mw-redirect">multi-core</a> <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM</a> <a href="/wiki/CPU" title="CPU" class="mw-redirect">CPU</a>, a <a href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU" class="mw-redirect">GPU</a>, and dedicated audio, video and image processors. Nvidia claimed that it consumes 2% of the energy of a typical CPU.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[133]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The navigation system uses <a href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS" class="mw-redirect">GPS</a> and a mix of Garmin and Google Maps route guidance. The map display on the 17-inch screen requires a constant Internet connection, so navigation is limited in areas without mobile network coverage. The Nav on the instrument panel is loaded on the car and does not need Internet access to function.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[134]</a></sup> Update 6.2 features automatic nav guidance to charging stations if range is insufficient.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[135]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Enthusiasts have developed the Open Vehicle Monitoring System (<a href="/wiki/OVMS" title="OVMS">OVMS</a>) which allows the owner to remotely observe a variety of different vehicle operating parameters, such as battery state of charge, typically using a <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a>. Some switchgear used are Mercedes parts, such as window switches, cruise control lever, and drive selector.</p> 
     <p>According to Elon Musk, the Model S runs on the open-source <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2015shareholdermeeting_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015shareholdermeeting-142">[136]</a></sup> In 2014 <a href="/wiki/Autoblog_(website)" title="Autoblog (website)">Autoblog</a> reported that Tesla Models S owners had determined via the car's combined <a href="/wiki/On-board_diagnostics" title="On-board diagnostics">diagnostics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethernet" title="Ethernet">Ethernet</a> port that a <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">Ubuntu</a> system controlling the central touchscreen is connected to the car's internal Ethernet.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[137]</a></sup> The same users determined that another Ubuntu system controlling the dashboard/navigation screen also is connected to the internal network, together with a third computer of unknown type with an unknown function.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[138]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3186" data-file-height="2124"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_rear_child_seats_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The Model S has an optional folding third row with rear-facing seats for two children secured with a racing-style five-point harness.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Key_(8406842279).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_Key_%288406842279%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Key_(8406842279).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The Model S key.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>All versions of the Model S have the same body and normally seat five passengers. An optional folding third row for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,500</span> becomes a rear-facing two-place child seat. The option includes a stronger rear bumper.<sup id="cite_ref-sciAbuild_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sciAbuild-111">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gcsafe_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcsafe-114">[108]</a></sup> Each third row seat has a racing-style five-point harness for passengers over 37&nbsp;in (0.94&nbsp;m) tall and weighing between 35 to 77&nbsp;lb (16 to 35&nbsp;kg). Cargo space is available under the front hood (which Tesla called a "frunk," a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "front trunk.") The optional third row gives the greatest passenger capacity of any electric vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[139]</a></sup> In October 2014 the upgraded Model S P85D, D for dual, was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[140]</a></sup> The upgraded version features not one but two electric motors, one driving the rear wheels as in prior versions, and one the front wheels. Safety features are enhanced also, for example with partial auto-pilot functions. The dual motor version will be available also for the basic 85 kWh versions for around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4,000</span> more in price. The rear wheel drive version of the P85 was removed, and the dual motor option is not available for the 60 kWh version.<sup id="cite_ref-David_Noland_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_Noland-63">[63]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 2015 model year update introduced <a href="/wiki/Electromechanical_brake" title="Electromechanical brake" class="mw-redirect">electromechanical brakes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[141]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicle_warranty_and_maintenance">Vehicle warranty and maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Vehicle warranty and maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The Model S is covered by a 4-year, 50,000&nbsp;mi (80,000&nbsp;km) limited warranty,<sup id="cite_ref-teslaspecs_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teslaspecs-148">[142]</a></sup> that includes all standard equipment, the transmission and the complete powertrain (excluding tires).<sup id="cite_ref-teslaservice_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teslaservice-149">[143]</a></sup> The warranty can be extended an additional 4 years or 50,000 miles (80,000&nbsp;km) beyond the original terms for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4,000</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-teslaservice_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teslaservice-149">[143]</a></sup> Warranty coverage includes a complementary loaner car—a Performance 85 or Tesla Roadster—when service is required.<sup id="cite_ref-teslablog_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teslablog-150">[144]</a></sup> In April 2013, Tesla announced that a previously mandatory <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$600</span> annual vehicle inspection and maintenance fee would be made optional, and would not be required to maintain warranty coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-teslablog_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teslablog-150">[144]</a></sup> If chosen, the fee covers a complete inspection, tire alignment, new brake pads, hardware upgrades and miscellaneous other maintenance items as needed.</p> 
     <p>The battery and drive unit are covered for eight years or 125,000 miles (200,000&nbsp;km in metric countries) for the 60&nbsp;kWh base model, or eight years and unlimited distance for all 70 and 85&nbsp;kWh models.<sup id="cite_ref-TMOptions_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMOptions-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NAwarranty_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAwarranty-151">[145]</a></sup> The unconditional battery warranty covers everything except deliberate damage, even including user error.<sup id="cite_ref-CNNmoney_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNmoney-152">[146]</a></sup> However, loss of battery capacity over time or usage is not covered under warranty.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="how does it differ from warranty – percentage of allowable degradation? (March 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-NAwarranty_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAwarranty-151">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QuickGuide_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuickGuide-153">[147]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_footprint">Environmental footprint</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environmental footprint">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In February 2014, the Automotive Science Group (ASG) published the result of a study conducted to <a href="/wiki/Life-cycle_assessment" title="Life-cycle assessment">assess the life-cycle</a> of over 1,300 automobiles across nine categories sold in North America. The study ranked the Model S as the best environmental performer in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Full-size_car" title="Full-size car">full-size cars</a> category.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[148]</a></sup> Based on the assessment of life-cycle environmental footprint, the study concluded that the increased environmental impacts of manufacturing the vehicle are more than offset with increased environmental performance during operation. For the assessment, the study used the average electricity mix of the U.S. grid in 2014. The <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> had the smallest life-cycle environmental footprint of any model year 2014 automobile available in the North American market.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[149]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tesla_stations">Tesla stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tesla stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg/220px-Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg/330px-Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg/440px-Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Charging_Tesla_Model_S_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Tesla Model S charging at the Supercharger network station in 
        <a href="/wiki/Newark,_Delaware" title="Newark, Delaware">Newark, Delaware</a>, United States.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg/220px-Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg/330px-Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg/440px-Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2027" data-file-height="1316"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Tesla_Model_S_Zoutelande_dunes_Holland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Tesla Model S charging at a public charging station in 
        <a href="/wiki/Zoutelande" title="Zoutelande">Zoutelande</a>, the Netherlands.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_station" title="Tesla station">Tesla station</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In 2012, Tesla began building a network of 480-volt <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">charging stations</a> to facilitate long-distance travel. In June 2013 Tesla announced that existing and future stations would become <a href="/wiki/Tesla_station" title="Tesla station">Tesla stations</a>, with facilities to support under-two-minute battery pack swaps. As of early October 2014, 115 stations were operating in the United States, 71 in Europe and 23 in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-USModelS18K_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USModelS18K-156">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tesla_Motors_Supercharger_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla_Motors_Supercharger-157">[151]</a></sup> The Tesla network is usable only by Tesla vehicles, which are engineered for compatibility.</p> 
     <p>The first Supercharger corridor opened in October 2012 with six stations placed along routes connecting San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tahoe" title="Lake Tahoe">Lake Tahoe</a>, Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC092512_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC092512-158">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HC121012_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HC121012-159">[153]</a></sup> A second corridor opened in December 2012 connecting Washington, D.C., New York City, and <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>; it includes three stations located in highway rest areas in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT122112_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT122112-160">[154]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first Tesla stations in Europe opened in Norway in August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperchargerNor_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperchargerNor-161">[155]</a></sup> Tesla next focused on Germany and the Netherlands, with plans to cover both countries by mid-2014. Switzerland, Belgium, Austria, Denmark and Luxembourg were to be covered by the end of 2014. Stations were to be within 200&nbsp;mi (320&nbsp;km) for about 90% of the population in France, England, Wales and Sweden by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-3Q2013Report_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3Q2013Report-162">[156]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supercharger">Supercharger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Supercharger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The Supercharger is a proprietary DC rapid-charging station that provides up to 135&nbsp;kW of power, giving 85&nbsp;kWh vehicles an additional 180&nbsp;mi (290&nbsp;km) of range in about 30 minutes. In the West Coast corridor the Superchargers's grid access is assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar</a> <a href="/wiki/Carport" title="Carport">carport</a> system (some including a battery of a few hundred kWh)<sup id="cite_ref-ingSup_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ingSup-163">[157]</a></sup> provided by <a href="/wiki/SolarCity" title="SolarCity">SolarCity</a>. Eventually, all Tesla stations will be assisted by solar power.</p> 
     <p>Supercharging hardware is now a standard on all vehicles sold by Tesla Motors. The Roadster is not compatible.<sup id="cite_ref-GCC092512_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCC092512-158">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HC121012_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HC121012-159">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT122112_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT122112-160">[154]</a></sup> In early November 2013, Tesla reported that 90% of its customers had opted for supercharging capability.<sup id="cite_ref-3Q2013Report_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3Q2013Report-162">[156]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_swapping">Battery swapping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Battery swapping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Tesla designed its Model S to allow fast battery swapping, which also facilitates vehicle assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[158]</a></sup> In June 2013, Tesla announced their goal to deploy a <a href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping" class="mw-redirect">battery swapping</a> station in Tesla stations. At a demonstration Tesla showed a battery swap operation taking just over 90 seconds, about half the time it takes to refill an empty gas tank.<sup id="cite_ref-Swapping01_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swapping01-165">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Swapping02_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swapping02-166">[160]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg/300px-Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg" width="300" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg/450px-Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg/600px-Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="3120" data-file-height="1044"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_charging_station_with_solar_collector_trimmed.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Panoramic view of Tesla Supercharger rapid charging station in 
        <a href="/wiki/Tejon,_California" title="Tejon, California">Tejon Ranch, California</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Battery swapping was to be deployed along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5_in_California" title="Interstate 5 in California">Interstate 5 in California</a> to allow travel from San Francisco to Los Angeles. These were to be followed by the Washington, DC to Boston corridor. Each swapping station costs <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500,000</span> and stocks about 50 batteries. The service would be offered for the price of about 15 US gallons (57&nbsp;l; 12&nbsp;imp&nbsp;gal) of gasoline at the current local rate, around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$60</span> to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$80</span> at June 2013 prices. Owners can pick up their original battery pack fully charged on the return trip, which is included in the swap fee. Tesla would also offer the option to keep the swapped battery for a fee or to receive the original pack from Tesla for a fee. Pricing has not been determined.<sup id="cite_ref-Swapping01_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swapping01-165">[159]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Tesla's only battery swap station is located at Harris Ranch, California, and was available for pilot testing in late December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[161]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Tesla says they have hundreds of cars in the battery swap program, although few owners are interested in using the service.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[162]</a></sup> In June 2015, Tesla said that it was unlikely that more battery swap stations would be added due to lack of demand for battery swaps costing around $60 when supercharging is included free with most models.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[163]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editions">Editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Editions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Tesla allocated the first 1,000 units to its Signature and Signature Performance limited edition configurations, equipped with the 85&nbsp;kWh battery pack, and priced in the U.S. at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$95,400</span> and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,400</span> respectively, not including any applicable <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles#United_States" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">U.S. federal and local government tax credits and incentives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GCR062112_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCR062112-170">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT050611_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT050611-171">[165]</a></sup> As of July 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the base Model S starts at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$75,000</span> with a 70&nbsp;kWh battery pack and goes up to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,000</span> for the performance model with the 85&nbsp;kWh pack before any government subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-my.teslamotors.com_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-my.teslamotors.com-65">[65]</a></sup> Tesla does not make a <a href="/wiki/Convertible" title="Convertible">convertible</a> Model S.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[167]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A custom Model S was designed for the <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_Preservation_Society" title="Oceanic Preservation Society">Oceanic Preservation Society</a> in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Obscura_Digital" title="Obscura Digital" class="mw-redirect">Obscura Digital</a>, and was used to project images of endangered animals to help educate the public about the <a href="/wiki/Holocene_mass_extinction" title="Holocene mass extinction" class="mw-redirect">Holocene mass extinction</a>, as featured in the 2015 documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Racing_Extinction" title="Racing Extinction">Racing Extinction</a></i>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_and_markets">Sales and markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sales and markets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global">Global</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Global">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1328"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_first_deliveries.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Model S first retail deliveries ceremony at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Factory" title="Tesla Factory">Tesla Factory</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_California" title="Fremont, California">Fremont, California</a>, held on June 22, 2012.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Tesla Motors reported 520 reservations for the Model S during the first week they were available<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[168]</a></sup> and as of 31 December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> over 15,000 net reservations (after deliveries and cancellations) had been received by year-end.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2012_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2012-175">[169]</a></sup> The special edition Model S Signature model was sold out before deliveries began in June 2012, and according to Tesla Motors all models were sold out for that year shortly after. A car ordered in May 2012 would be delivered in early to mid-2013.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[171]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Initially Tesla expected to reach global sales of 35,000 units in 2014, but in November 2014 reduced its sales target to 33,000 units due to a deficit in production of 2,000 units during the third quarter of 2014. The company expected its annual production to increase by over 50% in 2014 to 35,000 units, and another increase of 50% in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla3Q2014_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla3Q2014-178">[172]</a></sup> Tesla Motors set a target of between 50,000 and 52,000 deliveries for Model S and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_X" title="Tesla Model X">Model X</a> cars in 2015, and delivered 50,658 units.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla092015_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla092015-179">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup> Tesla plans to deliver 80,000 to 90,000 new Model S and Model X vehicles in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>2012</b></p> 
     <p>U.S. deliveries began June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-MSlaunch_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSlaunch-10">[10]</a></sup> Deliveries of the 60&nbsp;kWh model were rescheduled from November 2012 to January/February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Deliver4060_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deliver4060-181">[175]</a></sup> A total of 2,650 cars were delivered in North America in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2012_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2012-182">[176]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>2013</b></p> 
     <p>During the first six months of 2013, 10,050 were delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla1Q2013_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla1Q2013-183">[177]</a></sup> The Model S was released in Europe in early August 2013, and the first deliveries took place in Norway, Switzerland and the Netherlands,<sup id="cite_ref-DeliveryEU_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeliveryEU-184">[178]</a></sup> and by November 2013, the Model S was on sale in 20 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-3Q2013Report_162-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3Q2013Report-162">[156]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Sales totaled about 22,477 units in North America and Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla2013Sales_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla2013Sales-185">[179]</a></sup> surpassing Tesla's annual sales target of 21,500 units.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS25K_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS25K-186">[180]</a></sup> Global cumulative sales passed the 25,000 unit milestone in December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS25K_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS25K-186">[180]</a></sup> By the end of 2013, according to <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, Norway and Switzerland became the company's largest per capita sales markets.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[181]</a></sup></p>

     <p><b>2014</b></p> 
     <p>Retail deliveries in China began in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaFirst_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaFirst-188">[182]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">right-hand-drive model</a> was released in the UK in June 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-UKfirst_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKfirst-189">[183]</a></sup> followed by Hong Kong in July 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-1stHK_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1stHK-190">[184]</a></sup> and Japan in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[185]</a></sup> Deliveries in Australia began in December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[186]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Global cumulative sales of the Model S passed the 50,000 unit mark in October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS75K_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS75K-193">[187]</a></sup> A total of 31,655 units were sold worldwide in 2014, allowing the Model S to rank as the world's second best selling plug-in electric vehicle after the <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Top102014_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top102014-22">[22]</a></sup> In 2014 about 55% of Model S deliveries took place in North America (~17,410), 30% in Europe (~9,497), and 15% in the Asia-Pacific market (~4,748).<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2014_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2014-194">[188]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>2015</b></p> 
     <p>A total of 21,577 units were sold worldwide during the first half of 2015, of which, 11,532 were delivered during the second quarter alone, up about 52% over the same quarter the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS2Q2015_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS2Q2015-195">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ModelS062015_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS062015-196">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tesla1Q2015_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla1Q2015-197">[191]</a></sup> As of June 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Model S was sold in 30 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS2Q2015_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS2Q2015-195">[189]</a></sup> A total of 11,597 Model S cars were delivered during the third quarter, up about 49% over the same quarter in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla092015_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla092015-179">[173]</a></sup> A total of 17,272 Model S were delivered during the fourth quarter, up 76% over the same quarter the previous year, and setting a new record for the most cars delivered in a quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ModelS4Q2015_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS4Q2015-198">[192]</a></sup> Global Model S sales passed the 100,000 unit milestone in December 2015, three years and a half after its introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelS100K_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelS100K-20">[20]</a></sup> A total of 50,446 Model S sedans were sold globally in 2015, allowing the Model S to rank as the world's best-selling plug-in electric car in 2015, ahead of the Nissan Leaf (about 43,000 units).<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top2015Global_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top2015Global-21">[21]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of December 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 107,228 Model S sedans have been sold worldwide since its introduction, ranking as the world's second best selling plug-in car ever after the Nissan Leaf (200,000).<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top2015Global_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top2015Global-21">[21]</a></sup> The United States is the leading market with 63,161 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-199">[193]</a></sup> Norway is the Model S largest overseas market,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-200">[194]</a></sup> with 10,062 new units registered,<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2013_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2013-201">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OFV2014_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFV2014-202">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OFV2015_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFV2015-203">[197]</a></sup> followed by China with 5,524 units registered through September 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-China092015_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China092015-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-China2014_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2014-204">[198]</a></sup> and the Netherlands with 4,462 units registered at the end of December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-RAISales2012_13_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales2012_13-205">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RAISales2014_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales2014-206">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RAISales2015_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales2015-207">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nether2012_15_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nether2012_15-208">[202]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_selling_countries">Top selling countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Top selling countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
