     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia.2FPacific">Asia/Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Asia/Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><b>Australia</b></p> 
     <p>The first nine units were delivered in Sydney on December 9, 2014. Tesla Motors also opened its first store and service centre in <a href="/wiki/St_Leonards,_New_South_Wales" title="St Leonards, New South Wales">St Leonards</a>, and its first Supercharger station at <a href="/wiki/Pyrmont,_New_South_Wales" title="Pyrmont, New South Wales">Pyrmont</a> in December 2014. Initially, only two versions were available, the 60 starting at <span style="white-space: nowrap">A$91,400</span>, and the 85 starting at <span style="white-space: nowrap">A$103,400</span> before any options, stamp duty and the Australian luxury car tax (LCT). The Model S P85D, starting at <span style="white-space: nowrap">A$133,500</span>, had deliveries scheduled to begin in June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[224]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of December 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 65 Model S cars were registered in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> and only four in <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Australia2014_1Q2015_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australia2014_1Q2015-237">[225]</a></sup> At the end of March 2015, registrations totaled 119 in New South Wales and 54 in Victoria. Although there were no sales figures reported for Tesla in other states, the combined sales of these two states alone were enough for the Model S to rank as the top selling all-electric car in the country for the first quarter of 2015, ahead of the BMW i3 (46) and the Nissan Leaf (31).<sup id="cite_ref-Australia2014_1Q2015_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australia2014_1Q2015-237">[225]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>China</b></p> 
     <p>The first deliveries took place on April 22, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaFirst_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaFirst-188">[182]</a></sup> The Model S has the same standard equipment as the continental European version, but was adapted to provide larger back seats because the car was expected to be driven by a <a href="/wiki/Chauffeur" title="Chauffeur">chauffeur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla3Q2013_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla3Q2013-238">[226]</a></sup> Only two versions with an 85&nbsp;kWh battery pack are available in the Chinese market, standard and performance.<sup id="cite_ref-PriceChina_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PriceChina-239">[227]</a></sup> Pricing starts at CN¥734,000 (~US$121,200),<sup id="cite_ref-PriceChina_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PriceChina-239">[227]</a></sup> similar to the US, adding only taxes and transportation costs. Comparable luxury cars cost more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$180,000</span> in the Chinese market.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[229]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Chinese sales up to June 2014 were estimated between 1,000 to 1,300 units.<sup id="cite_ref-China2Q2014_01_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2Q2014_01-242">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-China2Q2014_02_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2Q2014_02-243">[231]</a></sup> JLWarren Capital, an equity firm, estimated that about 2,800 Tesla Model S cars have been imported to China by mid September 2014, but only 432 had received the license plates.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaModelS_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaModelS-244">[232]</a></sup> According to a Tesla spokesman, the major reasons for the discrepancy could be that registration rules were holding deliveries in Shanghai, and Tesla only recently was able to start delivering the electric cars to customers who bought them in Shanghai. Secondly, many Chinese customers have delayed taking possession of their Model S car while waiting for the government to add the Tesla to the list of electric vehicles exempt from its 8% to 10% purchase tax.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaModelS_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaModelS-244">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[233]</a></sup> As of December 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Tesla had imported 4,800 Model S cars, but only 2,499 of those vehicles were registered for road use in China.<sup id="cite_ref-China2014_204-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2014-204">[198]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Tesla's CEO expressed disappointment with the Chinese sales, as stock continued to be high by early 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[234]</a></sup> As sales improved, Model S sales reached 2,147 units representing an 80% share of the imported plug-in hybrid or electric car segment in China for the first half of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-China062015_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China062015-247">[235]</a></sup> Sales totaled 3,025 units during the first nine months of 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-China092015_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China092015-46">[46]</a></sup> for cumulative registrations of 5,524 units through September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-China092015_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China092015-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-China2014_204-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China2014-204">[198]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Hong Kong</b></p> 
     <p>Sales of the Model S began in July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-1stHK_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1stHK-190">[184]</a></sup> After the introduction of the Model S, sales of all-electric cars took off in Hong Kong. Thanks to the tax waiver and other government incentives, the Model S price is very competitive in the luxury car segment, about half the price of other high-end models. While the after tax price of the Model S 70D is HK$619,000, a <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_E-Class_(W212)" title="Mercedes-Benz E-Class (W212)">Mercedes-Benz E 200 Premium Edition</a> costs HK$1,009,500.<sup id="cite_ref-QuatzHK_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuatzHK-248">[236]</a></sup> As of July 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Model S is the top selling all-electric car in the territory with about 70% of the registered stock of EVs, about 1,720 units.<sup id="cite_ref-QuatzHK_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuatzHK-248">[236]</a></sup> According to Tesla, as of June 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Hong Kong has the world's highest density of <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors#Supercharger_network" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla superchargers</a>, with eight stations comprising a total of 36 supercharger stalls. This infrastructure allows most Model S owners to have a supercharger within 20 minutes' drive.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[237]</a></sup> Sales totaled 2,221 units in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-HK2015_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HK2015-219">[210]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_delivery_to_H%C3%B8yres_Nikolai_Astrup_in_Norway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The first European deliveries took place at Tesla's store in 
        <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> in August 2013.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Retail deliveries began in Europe in early August 2013, in Norway, Switzerland and the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-DeliveryEU_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeliveryEU-184">[178]</a></sup> The two biggest markets for the Model S in Europe are Norway and the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-TopMarkets_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopMarkets-250">[238]</a></sup> The Model S, with about 3,900 units sold, ended 2013 as the third-best selling all-electric car in Europe after the Nissan Leaf and the <a href="/wiki/Renault_Zoe" title="Renault Zoe">Renault Zoe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EU2013_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU2013-251">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EU122013_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU122013-252">[240]</a></sup> A total of 8,734 Model S cars were sold in 2014, representing a market share of 15.5% of new all-electric passenger car sales in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-Leaf2014EU_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaf2014EU-253">[241]</a></sup> and again allowing the Model S to rank as the third best selling all-electric car in Europe after the Leaf and the Zoe.<sup id="cite_ref-Leaf2014EU_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaf2014EU-253">[241]</a></sup> Accounting for sales during the first nine months of 2014, the Model S outsold the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_7_Series" title="BMW 7 Series">BMW 7 Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_XJ" title="Jaguar XJ">Jaguar XJ</a>, ranking second in the European <a href="/wiki/Full-size_car" title="Full-size car">full-size</a> <a href="/wiki/Luxury_vehicle" title="Luxury vehicle">luxury vehicle</a> segment after the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class">Mercedes-Benz S-Class</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[242]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>European Model S sales in 2015 totaled 15,169 units, ranking again third after the Zoe and very close behind the Leaf with 16.6% of the all-electric segment sales.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[243]</a></sup> The leading market was Norway with 3,243 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-EU3Q2015_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU3Q2015-256">[244]</a></sup> The Model S also ranked again second in the luxury car segment after the Mercedes-Benz S-Class.<sup id="cite_ref-EU3Q2015_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU3Q2015-256">[244]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Pricing</b></p> 
     <p>American and European standard equipment and options packages are the same. European prices are higher, due to <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rates</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">value-added tax</a> (VAT), plus transport costs, import duties and other country-specific costs. In most countries where the Model S is sold base prices for the 60&nbsp;kWh start at €72,600, and €83,150 for the 85&nbsp;kWh battery car. The 85&nbsp;kWh Performance, Signature, and Signature Performance trim levels are listed at €97,550, €101,400, and €110,950 respectively. Tesla offered a deduction of €1,700 to buyers who held a reservation by the end of December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[245]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[246]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Sales by country</b></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Czech Republic</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>A total of 23 units were sold during 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[247]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Denmark</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>During its first full month in the Danish market, the Model S was the top selling electric vehicle with 42 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[248]</a></sup> Sales were 112 units in 2013 and 460 in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark2013_15_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark2013_15-213">[205]</a></sup> Model S sales constituted 35% of the sales of luxury cars by mid 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[249]</a></sup> A Model S was tested as a taxi, but high price and low range made the project uneconomic.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pol2014-08_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pol2014-08-263">[251]</a></sup> When the AWD model was announced in Autumn 2014, used Model S were sold fast at high price.<sup id="cite_ref-pol2014-10_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pol2014-10-264">[252]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Due to a tax increased on electric cars due in 2016, as Parliament approved in October 2015 to phase out the tax exemption for electric vehicles, the Model S became the most sold car in Denmark in December 2015, with 1,248 cars delivered that month, out of 1,573 electric cars sold in December. This is the first time ever that an electric car is the best selling car in Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark2015_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark2015-19">[19]</a></sup> Cumulative sales in the country reached 3,308 units through December 2015, of which a record of 2,736 units were sold in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark2013_15_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark2013_15-213">[205]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Germany</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Model S customers in Germany are offered a free optional high speed tuning for <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> driving. The company announced that by November 2013 the first Tesla stations would open between Munich and Stuttgart, Munich and Zurich, Switzerland, and Cologne and Frankfurt. Tesla Motors planned to cover more than 50% of Germany by the end of March 2014, and 100% by the end of 2014. Germany would then have the most Superchargers per capita of any country. German stations would support 135 <a href="/wiki/KW" title="KW" class="mw-redirect">kW</a> charging.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[253]</a></sup> By late 2013 Tesla announced a goal to sell 10,000 Model S in Germany in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[254]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A total of 183 units were registered in the country during 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Ger2013Sales_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ger2013Sales-214">[206]</a></sup> Registrations totaled 815 units in 2014, representing 2.7% of the luxury segment sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesGer2014_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer2014-215">[207]</a></sup> As of November 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, cumulative registrations totaled 2,354 units.<sup id="cite_ref-Ger2013Sales_214-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ger2013Sales-214">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesGer2014_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer2014-215">[207]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesGer112015_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesGer112015-267">[255]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Netherlands</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>The first deliveries in the country occurred on August 22, 2013, at Tesla's European Distribution Center in <a href="/wiki/Tilburg" title="Tilburg">Tilburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tilburg_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tilburg-42">[42]</a></sup> A total of 1,194 units were sold in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-RAISales2012_13_205-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales2012_13-205">[199]</a></sup> After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_the_Netherlands#Government_incentives" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in the Netherlands">registration tax exemption</a>, sales fell significantly, and only 262 units were sold during the first four months of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-RAISales042014_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales042014-268">[256]</a></sup> Sales in 2015 totaled 1,805 units.<sup id="cite_ref-RAISales2015_207-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAISales2015-207">[201]</a></sup> The Model S leads the Dutch all-electric segment with 4,382 cars registered at the end of December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Nether2012_15_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nether2012_15-208">[202]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Norway</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>The first delivery of a Model S in Europe took place in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> on August 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[257]</a></sup> By the end of August 2013, Europe's first six charging stations were opened, in <a href="/wiki/Lyngdal" title="Lyngdal">Lyngdal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aurland" title="Aurland">Aurland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domb%C3%A5s" title="Dombås">Dombås</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gol,_Norway" title="Gol, Norway">Gol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundebru" title="Sundebru">Sundebru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lillehammer" title="Lillehammer">Lillehammer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SuperchargerNor_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuperchargerNor-161">[155]</a></sup> That month 186 units were delivered, ranking second among all-electric cars behind the Nissan Leaf (448 units).<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales082013_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales082013-270">[258]</a></sup> Sales surged in September totaling 616 units, beating the Leaf and achieving an overall new car market share of 5.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesNorway092013_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesNorway092013-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwayTop1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayTop1-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwayTop2_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayTop2-17">[17]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg/220px-Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg/330px-Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg/440px-Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Five_Tesla_Model_S_electric_cars_in_Norway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> As of December 2015
        <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Norway is the second largest Model S market by volume, with about 9.4% of cumulative global sales.
        <sup id="cite_ref-Top2015Global_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top2015Global-21">[21]</a></sup> Shown in 
        <a href="/wiki/Geiranger" title="Geiranger">Geiranger</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2013 a five-month waiting list emerged creating a used market, with <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10,000</span> to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20,000</span> premiums for a used model.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[260]</a></sup> Sales dropped to 98 units in October,<sup id="cite_ref-SalesNorway102013_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesNorway102013-273">[261]</a></sup> before jumping back to 527 units in November, ranking it number two in new car registrations after the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Volkswagen Golf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesNorway112013_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesNorway112013-274">[262]</a></sup> In December sales of 553 units made it the top-selling new car again and capturing a 4.9% market share of new car sales.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwayTop3_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayTop3-18">[18]</a></sup> With less than five months of sales, the Model S ranked 20th for the year with a market share of 1.4% of Norwegian new car sales, Tesla's largest in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-TopNorway2013_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopNorway2013-275">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[264]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Model S topped the monthly sales ranking for a third time in March 2014, with 1,493 units sold, breaking the 28-year-old monthly sales record, surpassing the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a>, which sold 1,454 units in May 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-Norway1Q2014_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway1Q2014-277">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[266]</a></sup> Sales totaled 2,056 Model S cars during the first quarter of 2014, making the Model S the best selling new car in Norway during this period. The Model S captured a 5.6% market share of new car sales and 38.8% of the new plug-in electric car segment during this quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-Norway1Q2014_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway1Q2014-277">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwayEVSales032014_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayEVSales032014-279">[267]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[268]</a></sup> By the end of 2014, the Model S ranked as the fifth best selling new car in the Norwegian market, with 4,040 units registered and a market share of 2.8% of new car sales in the country that year.<sup id="cite_ref-OFV2014_202-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFV2014-202">[196]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of July 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Norway ranked as Tesla's largest overseas market, with an average of 436 Model S sedans sold per month since August 2013. In comparison, the average in the United States is about 1,630 units delivered per month since the electric car went on sales in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-200">[194]</a></sup> Since its introduction, a total of 10,062 Model S new cars have sold in Norway through December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2013_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2013-201">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OFV2014_202-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFV2014-202">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OFV2015_203-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OFV2015-203">[197]</a></sup> Norway is the second largest Model S market by volume, with about 9.4% of cumulative global sales as of December 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-Top2015Global_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top2015Global-21">[21]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>Switzerland</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Retail deliveries began in August 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-DeliveryEU_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeliveryEU-184">[178]</a></sup> and a total of 213 units were registered in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesSwiss2013_15_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesSwiss2013_15-218">[209]</a></sup> The Model S, with 496 units registered, ranked as the top selling plug-in electric car in the country in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[269]</a></sup> With 835 units sold during the first seven months of 2015, the Model S outsold combined Swiss sales of the <a href="/wiki/Luxury_vehicle" title="Luxury vehicle">luxury</a> segment including such models as the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_S-Class" title="Mercedes S-Class" class="mw-redirect">Mercedes S-Class</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">Audi A8</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW_7_Series" title="BMW 7 Series">BMW 7 Series</a> during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[270]</a></sup> Cumulative Model S sales totaled 1,978 units up until October 2015, which includes units sold in <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesSwiss2013_15_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesSwiss2013_15-218">[209]</a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <b>United Kingdom</b>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Deliveries began in June 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-UKfirst_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKfirst-189">[183]</a></sup> and a total of 698 units were registered in the UK by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-UKcum1Q2015_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKcum1Q2015-283">[271]</a></sup> Pricing starts at <span class="nowrap">£54,380</span> before the <span class="nowrap">£5,000</span> <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_Car_Grant" title="Plug-in Car Grant" class="mw-redirect">Plug-in Car Grant</a>. Model S owners are also exempted from the <a href="/wiki/London_congestion_charge" title="London congestion charge">London congestion charge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[272]</a></sup> Cumulative registrations totaled 1,047 units at the end of June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-UKcum2Q2015_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKcum2Q2015-224">[214]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America_2">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><b>Canada</b></p> 
     <p>The first Model S sedans were delivered in December 2012. Cumulative sales totaled 3,590 units as of December 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and ranks as the second best-selling plug-in car in the country ever after the Chevrolet Volt (5,415) and ahead of the Nissan Leaf (3,198). The Model S was the top selling plug-in electric car in Canada in 2015 with 2,010 units sold.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesCanada2015_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesCanada2015-212">[204]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Mexico</b></p> 
     <p>Retail sales began in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> in December 2015. Initially, no Supercharger stations are available in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[273]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>United States</b></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Model_S,_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png/220px-Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png/330px-Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png/440px-Model_S%2C_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png 2x" data-file-width="1537" data-file-height="937"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Model_S,_as_imagined_by_the_WSJ.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Personalized delivery of a Tesla Model S in the U.S.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The first delivery took place on June 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[274]</a></sup> Deliveries for retail customers in the United States started on June 22, at a special event held at the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Factory" title="Tesla Factory">Tesla Factory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_California" title="Fremont, California">Fremont, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MSlaunch_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSlaunch-10">[10]</a></sup> The first 1,000 production units were Signature and Signature Performance limited editions equipped with an 85&nbsp;kWh battery pack.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2012_175-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2012-175">[169]</a></sup> Cumulative sales passed the 50,000 unit milestone in early July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-CumSales062015US_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CumSales062015US-287">[275]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>About 2,620 units were sold in the U.S. during 2012 out of 2,650 units delivered in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2012_175-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2012-175">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-199">[193]</a></sup> California is the largest American regional market for the Model S.<sup id="cite_ref-TopMarkets_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopMarkets-250">[238]</a></sup> In March 2013, Tesla reported the delivery of the 3,000th Model S in California, representing around 50% of US sales to that date.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[277]</a></sup> During the first quarter of 2013 the Model S ranked as the top selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicle</a> in the U.S. with about 4,900 units delivered, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> with 4,244 units.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla1Q2013_183-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla1Q2013-183">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PEVSales032013US_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVSales032013US-290">[278]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[279]</a></sup> During 2013, the Model S was listed as the least stolen car in the United States, with a theft rating of just 0.15 per 1,000 units produced. By comparison, the U.S. average is 3.51 cars stolen per 1,000 produced. The <a href="/wiki/Honda_Accord" title="Honda Accord">Honda Accord</a> was the most stolen car in the U.S. in 2013, with about 54,000 units, mostly models built in 2007 or before.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[280]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG/220px-Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG/330px-Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG/440px-Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Model_S_04_2015_SFO_2457.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> California is the top selling regional market of the Model S. Shown in San Francisco.
        <sup id="cite_ref-Calif_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calif-293">[281]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Edmunds.com" title="Edmunds.com">Edmunds.com</a>, between January and August 2013 the Model S achieved a high <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of new car sales among the U.S. most expensive <a href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">ZIP codes</a>, as rated by <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>, led by California. <a href="/wiki/Atherton,_California" title="Atherton, California">Atherton</a> ranked first with a 15.4% share, followed by <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos_Hills,_California" title="Los Altos Hills, California">Los Altos Hills</a> with 11.9%, and <a href="/wiki/Portola_Valley,_California" title="Portola Valley, California">Portola Valley</a> with 11.2%. During this period the Model S had the highest number of new passenger car registrations in 8 of the 25 most expensive American ZIP codes.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[282]</a></sup> With 8,347 units sold in 2013, it was the third-best selling luxury car in California (after the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_E-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz E-Class">Mercedes-Benz E-Class</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW_5_Series" title="BMW 5 Series">BMW 5 Series</a> sedans),<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[283]</a></sup> with a 9.8% share of the Californian luxury and sports segment.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[284]</a></sup> As of November 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Model S was available nationwide with California leading sales with a 48% share of national sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Calif_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calif-293">[281]</a></sup> During the first nine months of 2015, with 7,736 units registered, the Model S captured a 11.4% market share of the luxury and sports segment in California and ranked third after the Mercedes-Benz E-Class (8,583) and BMW 5 Series (8,207).<sup id="cite_ref-Calif3Q2015_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calif3Q2015-297">[285]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>American sales totaled about 18,650 units in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-298">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USModelS18K_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USModelS18K-156">[150]</a></sup> placing the Model S as the third selling plug-in electric car after the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> (23,094) and the Nissan Leaf (22,610).<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_199-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-199">[193]</a></sup> Also in 2013, the Model S was the top seller in the <a href="/wiki/Full-size_luxury_car" title="Full-size luxury car" class="mw-redirect">full-size luxury</a> <a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">sedan</a> category, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class">Mercedes-Benz S-Class</a> at 13,303.<sup id="cite_ref-USModelS18K_156-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USModelS18K-156">[150]</a></sup> In 2014, 16,689 Model S sedans were delivered, down 10.5% from 2013, but the electric sedan ranked again as the third best selling plug-in car in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_298-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-298">[286]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2015 the Model S ranked as the top selling plug-in electric car in the U.S, with 25,202 units sold surpassed both the Leaf (17,296) and the Volt (15,393).<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2015US_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2015US-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ModelSTop2015US_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSTop2015US-24">[24]</a></sup> The Model S was also the country's best-selling car in the large luxury segment among comparably priced four-door sedans, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class">Mercedes-Benz S-Class</a> (21,934) and <a href="/wiki/BMW_7_Series" title="BMW 7 Series">BMW 7 Series</a> (9,292).<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup> An estimated 63,161 Model S cars have been sold in the United States through December 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-Tesla4Q2015_180-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tesla4Q2015-180">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_199-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-199">[193]</a></sup> representing almost 60% of global total sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Top2015Global_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top2015Global-21">[21]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Retail sales model</b></p> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors#Business_model_and_US_automotive_dealership_disputes" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla sales model</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Tesla Motors sells its cars directly to consumers without creating a dealer network, as other manufacturers have done and as many states require by legislation. In support of its approach, the company has fought legal and legislative battles in Ohio, New Jersey, New York and other states.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[288]</a></sup> With law changes in recent years in New Jersey, New York, Maryland, Ohio, and Pennsylvania the Tesla direct sales model is permitted in 22 states as of March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[290]</a></sup> As of May 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the sales procedure in other states such as Texas is somewhat different with the Tesla salesperson being prevented from discussing prices, the actual sale having to be made online and the sales tax having to be paid up front. Delivery of a Tesla car to a Texas address is no different than in other states.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[291]</a></sup> Consequently, while Tesla showcases and sells its cars directly to the consumer in <i>Tesla Stores</i> abroad, it operates a mix of <i>Tesla Stores</i> and <i>Tesla Galleries</i> in the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[292]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Pricing</b></p> 
     <p>In June 2012, the Model S Signature model was priced at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$95,400</span> and the Signature Performance model at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,400</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-GCR062112_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCR062112-170">[164]</a></sup> On November 29, 2012, Tesla announced an all model price increase of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2,500</span> for new reservations, starting January 1, 2013. The price of a pre-paid 60&nbsp;kWh replacement pack was <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10,000</span>, while the 85&nbsp;kWh pack was priced at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12,000</span>, in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013Price_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013Price-305">[293]</a></sup> As of June 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the model with the 60&nbsp;kWh pack begins at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$69,900</span>, the base model with the 85&nbsp;kWh pack starts at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$79,900</span>, and the P85 performance model at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$93,400</span>. As of April 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Model S begins at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$75,000</span> for the 70&nbsp;kWh dual-motor edition, <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$80,000</span> for the 85&nbsp;kWh single motor edition, <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$85,000</span> for the 85&nbsp;kWh dual-motor edition, and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105,000</span> for the 85&nbsp;kWh dual-motor performance edition. These prices do not reflect <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles#United_States" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">U.S. federal and local government tax credits or purchase incentives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TMOptions_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TMOptions-83">[83]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;max-width:229px"> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_(front_view)_Netherlands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg/225px-2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg/338px-2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg/450px-2014_Tesla_Motors_Model_S_%28front_view%29_Netherlands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3280"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Model S frontal view
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B,_rear_right.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg/225px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg" width="225" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg/338px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg/450px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_P85%2B%2C_rear_right.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5284" data-file-height="2728"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Model S rear view
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Model S is one of just a few cars to have ever achieved a 5-star safety rating from both Euro NCAP and the U.S. National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA). Only two other cars have earned the same recognition since 2011 (when the NHTSA introduced its latest rating scheme).<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[294]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="A self-published source used to back up a claim about third parties (October 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <table class="wikitable"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">NHTSA</a><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[295]</a></sup></th> 
        <th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Euro_NCAP" title="Euro NCAP">Euro NCAP</a><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[296]</a></sup></th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td>Overall</td> 
        <td><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="5/5 stars"><img alt="5/5 stars" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" title="5/5 stars" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="108" data-file-height="110"></span></td> 
        <td>Overall</td>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_crash_with_battery_fire">First crash with battery fire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: First crash with battery fire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle_fire_incidents#Tesla_Model_S" title="Plug-in electric vehicle fire incidents">Tesla Model S fire incidents</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The first widely reported Model S fire occurred several minutes after the vehicle hit metal debris on the <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_Route_167" title="Washington State Route 167">Washington State Route 167</a> highway in <a href="/wiki/Kent,_Washington" title="Kent, Washington">Kent, Washington</a> on October 1, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire01_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire01-309">[297]</a></sup> The driver "was able to exit the highway as instructed by the onboard alert system, bring the car to a stop and depart the vehicle without injury".<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire03_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire03-310">[298]</a></sup> He then contacted authorities and, while awaiting their arrival, smoke began coming out the front of the vehicle. The driver stated that he hit something while exiting the <a href="/wiki/HOV_lane" title="HOV lane" class="mw-redirect">HOV lane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire01_309-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire01-309">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[300]</a></sup> Tesla stated that the fire was caused by the "direct impact of a large metallic object to one of the 16 <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a> modules", and that by design, the modules were separated by firewalls, limiting the fire to "a small section in the front of the vehicle".<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire01_309-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire01-309">[297]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The module was evidently punctured by a "curved section" that fell off a truck and was recovered near the accident. Tesla stated that the debris punched a 3-inch (76&nbsp;mm) diameter hole through the .25-inch (6.4&nbsp;mm) armor plate under the vehicle, applying force of some 25 <a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">tons</a>. Built-in vents directed the flames away from the vehicle so that the fire did not enter the passenger compartment. According to Tesla, the firefighters followed standard procedure; using large amounts of water to extinguish the fire was correct,<sup id="cite_ref-Model_S_First_Responder_Guide_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Model_S_First_Responder_Guide-313">[301]</a></sup> however, puncturing the metal firewall to gain access to the fire also allowed the flames to spread to the front trunk.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire03_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire03-310">[298]</a></sup> Tesla also stated that because the battery pack contains "only about 10% of the energy contained in a gasoline tank", the effective combustion potential of a single module is only about 1% that of a conventional vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-ModelSfire03_310-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ModelSfire03-310">[298]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On October 24, 2013, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) announced, "After reviewing all available data, the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration has not found evidence at this time that would indicate the recent battery fire involving a Tesla Model S was the result of a vehicle safety defect or noncompliance with federal safety standards."<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[302]</a></sup> But the following month, the NHTSA opened a preliminary evaluation to determine "the potential risks associated with undercarriage strikes on model year 2013 Tesla Model S vehicles".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT11192013_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT11192013-315">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[304]</a></sup> On March 28, 2014, NHTSA closed its investigation, claiming that the new titanium underbody shield and aluminum deflector plates, along with increased ground clearance, "should reduce both the frequency of underbody strikes and the resultant fire risk".<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[305]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_fires">Subsequent fires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Subsequent fires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On November 6, 2013 another fire broke out after a Model S struck a <a href="/wiki/Tow_hitch" title="Tow hitch">tow hitch</a> on the roadway, causing damage beneath the vehicle.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT112013_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT112013-318">[306]</a></sup> The incidents led Tesla to extend its vehicle warranty to cover fire damage and to apply a software update to increase ground clearance when operating at highway speed.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT11192013_315-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT11192013-315">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[307]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another fire incident took place in Toronto, Canada, in early February 2014. The Model S was parked in a garage and was not charging when the fire started. The origin of the fire is undetermined.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[308]</a></sup> According to Tesla "in this particular case, we don't yet know the precise cause, but have definitively determined that it did not originate in the battery, the charging system, the adapter or the electrical receptacle, as these components were untouched by the fire".<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[309]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Starting with vehicle bodies manufactured as of 6 March 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, all units were outfitted with a triple underbody shield. Existing cars were retrofitted upon request or as part of a normally scheduled service.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[310]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[311]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On 1 January 2016, a 2014 Model S caught fire in Norway while supercharging unsupervised. The vehicle was totally destroyed but nobody was injured.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[314]</a></sup> The fire was slow, and the owner had time to unplug the car and retrieve possesions.<sup id="cite_ref-vg18March2016_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vg18March2016-327">[315]</a></sup> An investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Accident_Investigation_Board_Norway" title="Accident Investigation Board Norway">Norwegian Accident Investigation Board (AIBN)</a> indicated that the fire originated in the car, but was otherwise inconclusive.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[316]</a></sup> In March 2016, Tesla stated that their own investigation into the incident concluded that the fire was caused by a short circuit in the vehicle's distribution box, but that the amount of damage prevented them from determining the exact cause.<sup id="cite_ref-vg18March2016_327-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vg18March2016-327">[315]</a></sup> Tesla stated that the Supercharger detected the short circuit and deactivated, and a future Model S software update would stop the vehicle from charging if a short circuit is detected.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[317]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recalls">Recalls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Recalls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On November 20, 2015, Tesla announced a voluntary worldwide recall of all of its 90,000 Model S vehicles, in order to check for a possible defect in the cars' front seat belt assemblies. The problem was raised in early November by one customer in Europe. Tesla's resulting investigation was unable to identify a root cause for the failure, and the company decided to examine every single car. Tesla reported that there have been no accidents or injuries related to the problem.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[319]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>2013 AutoGuide.com Reader's Choice Car of the Year<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[320]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>2013 <a href="/wiki/World_Car_of_the_Year" title="World Car of the Year">World Green Car of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[321]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Automobile_Magazine" title="Automobile Magazine" class="mw-redirect">Automobile Magazine</a>'s 2013 Car of the Year, a unanimous decision.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Automobile_of_the_Year:_Tesla_Model_S_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Automobile_of_the_Year:_Tesla_Model_S-334">[322]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/CNET" title="CNET">CNET</a> Tech Car of the Year for 2012<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[323]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a></i> gave the Model S a score of 103 out of 100, its highest ever. The Model S broke the rating scale of Consumer Reports during its most recent test.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[324]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Consumer Reports'</i> 2013 survey of owner satisfaction produced a score of 99 out of 100, "the highest the magazine has seen in years."<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[325]</a></sup> In 2014 the Model S topped for the second year in a row <i>Consumer Reports</i> survey of owner satisfaction. This time the Model S had a score of 98 out of 100.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[326]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Consumer Reports</i> found the Model S to be 'Best Overall' for 2014 across all 10 categories of cars, light trucks and SUVs, chosen from more than 260 vehicles the organization has recently tested. The magazine considers the Model S a "technological tour de force, while pricey, is brimming with innovation."<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[327]</a></sup> In 2015 they rated the Model S at 103 (breaking the scale).<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[329]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Green Car Reports' Best Car To Buy 2013<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[330]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Motor_Trend" title="Motor Trend">Motor Trend</a></i> 2013 <a href="/wiki/Motor_Trend_Car_of_the_Year" title="Motor Trend Car of the Year">Car of the Year</a>, also a unanimous decision and the first winner in the award's history to not be powered by an internal combustion engine.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Motor_Trend_Car_of_the_Year:_Tesla_Model_S_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Motor_Trend_Car_of_the_Year:_Tesla_Model_S-343">[331]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Natural_Resources_Canada" title="Natural Resources Canada">Natural Resources Canada</a> 2013 EcoENERGY for Vehicles Awards in the full-size category<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[332]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Science" title="Popular Science">Popular Science</a>'</i>s Auto Grand Award Winner Best of What's New list 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[333]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i> included the Model S in its list of the top 10 cars that changed the world published in December 2014, and also named the electric sedan the most important car of the last 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[334]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[335]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time Magazine</a></i> Best 25 Inventions of the Year 2012 award.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[336]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> Autos 2013 Car of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[337]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/American_Automobile_Association" title="American Automobile Association">American Automobile Association</a> Green Car Guide 2015, top spot (P85D).<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[338]</a></sup> The Model S also won the 2014 AAA Green Car Guide.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[339]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distance_records">Distance records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Distance records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>As of August 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the distance record is 728.7 kilometres (452.8&nbsp;mi) in a Model S on a single charge. It was made by Norwegian Bjørn Nyland and his friend on a flat stretch with low traffic around the supercharger in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B8dekro" title="Rødekro">Rødekro</a>, Denmark. They used <a href="/wiki/Energy-efficient_driving" title="Energy-efficient driving">hypermiling</a> techniques such as front motor only, low speed (39&nbsp;km/h) and no airconditioning.<sup id="cite_ref-NylandDist_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NylandDist-352">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[341]</a></sup> The previous record was 425.8 miles (685.3&nbsp;km), made overnight on February 14, 2013 by Bruno Bowden.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[342]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[343]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[344]</a></sup> The first record of 423.5 miles (681.6&nbsp;km) was set during November 2012 by David and Adam Metcalf.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[346]</a></sup> These attempts were inspired by a blog written by Elon Musk about the planned range and efficiency of the Tesla Model S, offering a prize for anyone exceeding 400 miles (640&nbsp;km) on a single charge, where it was estimated the 85 kwh model could do it by driving at a constant 36&nbsp;mph (58&nbsp;km/h) under ideal conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[347]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Range_limitation">Range limitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Range limitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On February 8, 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> published a review by John M. Broder about a trip between Washington, D.C., and Boston using Tesla's Supercharger network. At the time it included only two stations on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>. Broder made a variety of critical claims about the battery's performance in cold weather and the distance between charging stations. The trip ended with the Model S carried by a <a href="/wiki/Flatbed_truck" title="Flatbed truck">flatbed truck</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Milford,_Connecticut" title="Milford, Connecticut">Milford, Connecticut</a>, station.<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[348]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Tesla responded by publishing logs of the vehicle's charge levels and driving speed that contradicted Broder's account on several factual details.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[349]</a></sup> Tesla implied that Broder's behavior forced the car to fail. Broder replied to the criticism in a blog post and suggested that the speed discrepancies may have been because the car had been equipped with <a href="/wiki/Wheel_sizing#Wheel_size" title="Wheel sizing">19-inch wheels rather than the specified 21-inch wheels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[350]</a></sup> In the midst of the controversy, a <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> reporter recreated Broder's trip without exhausting the battery. However, two key differences distinguished the two journeys. The weather was about 10&nbsp;°F (6&nbsp;°C) warmer and CNN did the trip in one day; the <i>Times</i> let the car sit overnight without being plugged in.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[351]</a></sup> A reporter from <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> also recreated the trip in one day without incidents.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[352]</a></sup> One week later, a group of Tesla owners recreated Broder's trip without problems. One owner was delayed because his car failed to charge and required two <a href="/wiki/Firmware" title="Firmware">firmware</a> updates.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[354]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On February 18, 2013, <i>New York Times</i> <a href="/wiki/Public_Editor" title="Public Editor" class="mw-redirect">Public Editor</a> Margaret Sullivan published an editorial stating that Broder took "casual and imprecise notes" of his test drive and did not use good judgment, but she maintained that the article was done in good faith. She also claimed that Broder's vehicle logs were "sometimes quite misleading."<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[355]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[357]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In July and September 2014 tests performed by an independent German car magazine in cooperation with the TÜV (German Association for Technical Inspection) and Tesla owners seemed to reveal issues with the battery's performance. According to the magazine, Tesla did not take up the invitation to repeat the test, and also seemed to refuse to offer vehicles for a second test.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[358]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[359]</a></sup> A test performed by another German publication ("<a href="/wiki/Die_Welt" title="Die Welt">Die Welt</a>") supported the findings.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">[360]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NHTSA_safest_car">NHTSA safest car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: NHTSA safest car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>On August 19, 2013, based on NHTSA safety ratings, a Tesla press release claimed that the Model S had achieved the best safety rating of any car ever tested. Tesla stated, "NHTSA does not publish a star rating above 5, however safety levels better than 5 stars <i>are</i> captured in the overall Vehicle Safety Score (VSS) provided to manufacturers, where the Model S achieved a new combined record of 5.4 stars."<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[361]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[362]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[363]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[364]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[365]</a></sup> However, a few days later NHTSA rebutted Tesla's claim, explaining that the rating for the Model S was equal to any other car receiving 5-stars, and claiming that the carmaker did not follow its advertising guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[366]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[367]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[368]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_dissipation_when_not_in_use">Power dissipation when not in use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Power dissipation when not in use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Older versions of the system software suffered from power drain issues when the car wasn't being used, with the batteries losing 4.5 kWh overnight (known commonly as "vampire drain").<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[369]</a></sup> System software v5.8 (v1.49.30), released December 12, 2013, reduced overnight energy loss substantially, to 1.1&nbsp;kWh per night, or around 3 miles.<sup id="cite_ref-vampire_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vampire-71">[71]</a></sup> In January 2014, Bjørn Nyland, a Model S owner in Norway, recorded a range loss of approximately 20% during a 27-day extended vacation, an indicated range loss of 63 miles (101&nbsp;km), or 2.3 miles (3.7&nbsp;km) per day, while stored in frigid temperatures without any charging cable attached.<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[370]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_Reports_withdraws_recommendation">Consumer Reports withdraws recommendation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Consumer Reports withdraws recommendation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In October 2015, two months after naming the Tesla 'the best car ever tested,' Consumer Reports declined to give the Tesla Model S a "recommended" designation, citing too many complaints from owners. Complaints ranged from minor, such as misaligned doors and squeaky body, to severe - things like total drive train replacement and inoperable door handles. Tesla's shares dropped 15%, both because of the magazine's cut and because of concerns over the Tesla Model X luxury SUV.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[371]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[372]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_discrepancy">Power discrepancy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Power discrepancy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>The P85D "Insane" was widely reported to have 691 horsepower,<sup id="cite_ref-mtLudi_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtLudi-385">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-S2015-03-11_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S2015-03-11-386">[374]</a></sup> but some owners reported 20% less power on <a href="/wiki/Dynamometer" title="Dynamometer">dynamometer</a> in various circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-dtDP_387-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dtDP-387">[375]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hcDP_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hcDP-388">[376]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Manufacturers are required by EU law to display power "at full setting of the power controller" (from an external DC source when performing laboratory vehicle approval), but not necessarily to show power limited by battery. Other equipment must be removed, or their power added to the measurement.<sup id="cite_ref-straubDP_389-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straubDP-389">[377]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[378]</a></sup> Actual power available depends on circumstances,<sup id="cite_ref-straubDP_389-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-straubDP-389">[377]</a></sup> as it does for piston cars<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[379]</a></sup> which until 1972 could be 25–30% less than given.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[380]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[381]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of November 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Tesla website shows battery-limited combined 463&nbsp;hp for P85D (532&nbsp;hp for "Ludicrous").<sup id="cite_ref-S2015-11-02_394-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-S2015-11-02-394">[382]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dtDP_387-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dtDP-387">[375]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tesla_Model_S&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
